style="font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;color:#3c4043;font-weight:bold;">Q1 2018 impact from equity securities*</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;color:#3c4043;">Our Q1 2018 financial results were affected by a new accounting standard (ASU 2016-01) that changes the way companies account for equity security investments. As a result, all gains and losses, unrealized and realized, on equity security investments are recognized in OI&amp;E on the income statement. Performance fees related to the equity security gains in Q1 2018 were accrued in the period. Income tax expense on the equity security gains was offset by the release of a deferred tax asset valuation allowance. The presentation of this financial information is not intended to be considered in isolation or as a substitute for, or superior to, the financial information prepared and presented in accordance with GAAP.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:8px;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;color:#3c4043;">We use these non-GAAP financial measures for financial and operational decision-making and as a means to evaluate period-to-period comparisons. We believe that these non-GAAP financial measures provide meaningful supplemental information regarding our performance and liquidity by excluding certain items that may not be indicative of our recurring core business operating results, such as our revenues excluding the impact of foreign exchange rate movements and hedging activities. We believe that both management and investors benefit from referring to these non-GAAP financial measures in assessing our performance and when planning, forecasting, and analyzing future periods. These non-GAAP financial measures also facilitate management's internal comparisons to our historical performance and liquidity as well as comparisons to our competitors' operating results. We believe these non-GAAP financial measures are useful to investors both because (1) they allow for greater transparency with respect to key metrics used by management in its financial and operational decision-making and (2) they are used by our institutional investors and the analyst community to help them analyze the health of our business.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:8px;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;color:#3c4043;">There are a number of limitations related to the use of non-GAAP financial measures. We compensate for these limitations by providing specific information regarding the GAAP amounts excluded from these non-GAAP financial measures and evaluating these non-GAAP financial measures together with their relevant financial measures in accordance with GAAP.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:8px;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;color:#3c4043;">For more information on these non-GAAP financial measures, please see the tables captioned "Reconciliation from net cash provided by operating style="font-family:Arial;font-size:9pt;color:#3c4043;">)%</font></div></td></tr></table></div></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:8px;text-align:justify;font-size:9pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:9pt;color:#3c4043;font-style:italic;">Non-GAAP constant currency revenues and growth: </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:9pt;color:#3c4043;">We define non-GAAP constant currency revenues as total revenues excluding the impact of foreign exchange rate movements and hedging activities, and we use it to determine the constant currency revenue growth on year-on-year and quarter-on-quarter bases. Non-GAAP constant currency revenues are calculated by translating current quarter revenues using prior period exchange rates and excluding any hedging impact recognized in the current quarter. Constant currency revenue growth (expressed as a percentage) is calculated by determining the increase in current quarter non-GAAP constant currency revenues over prior period revenues, excluding any hedging impact recognized in the prior period.</font></div><div><br></div><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font <div><a name="sC54A1E2D7FEE33F929F2E9DE7EFCB751"></a></div><div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:8px;text-align:right;font-size:9pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:9pt;color:#3c4043;">Exhibit 99.2</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div></div><div><br></div><div style="line-height:132%;padding-bottom:24px;text-align:left;font-size:16pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:16pt;background-color:#ffffff;color:#3c4043;font-weight:bold;">A few new accounting, reporting, and disclosure items in our Q1 earnings </font></div><div style="line-height:138%;padding-bottom:12px;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;">In order to help you better understand our financial results for the first quarter of 2018 that we&#8217;ll report on Monday, April 23, we are sharing information about a few changes.</font></div><div style="line-height:138%;padding-left:0px;padding-bottom:12px;text-align:left;text-indent:0px;"><font style="padding-bottom:12px;text-align:left;font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;font-weight:bold;padding-right:48px;">&#8226;</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;font-weight:bold;">New accounting for equity security investments</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;">&#32;</font></div><div style="line-height:138%;padding-bottom:12px;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;">As of January 1, 2018, we were required to adopt a new accounting standard (ASU 2016-01) that changes the way companies account for equity security investments. Our equity security investments include both marketable equity securities (investments in publicly-traded companies) and non-marketable equity securities (investments in privately-held companies). </font></div><div style="line-height:138%;padding-bottom:12px;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;">Previously, marketable equity security investments were measured at fair value with unrealized gains and losses recognized on the balance sheet. Non-marketable equity security investments were measured at cost on the balance sheet.  Realized marketable and non-marketable gains and losses on our equity security investments were recognized in OI&amp;E on the income statement. </font></div><div style="line-height:138%;padding-bottom:12px;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;">Beginning in Q1 2018, non-marketable equity security investments will be measured at fair value on the balance sheet when transactions occur. Marketable equity securities will continue to be measured at fair value on the balance sheet. In addition to realized gains and losses, </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;font-weight:bold;">unrealized</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;">&#32;gains and losses on marketable and non-marketable equity security investments will also be recognized in OI&amp;E on the income statement. </font></div><div style="line-height:138%;padding-bottom:12px;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;">Market transactions for marketable equity securities occur daily in the stock market; transactions for non-marketable equity securities occur sporadically and are generally not within our control. As a result of this new accounting standard, we expect increased </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;font-style:italic;">volatility</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;">&#32;in OI&amp;E on the income statement.  </font></div><div style="line-height:138%;padding-bottom:12px;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;">Below is a summary of accounting treatment for realized and unrealized gains and losses: </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-bottom:12px;text-align:left;padding-left:0px;text-indent:0px;font-size:11pt;"><div style="padding-left:0px;text-indent:0px;line-height:normal;padding-top:10px;"><table style="page-break-after:always"><div></div><div><br></div><div style="line-height:138%;padding-left:0px;padding-bottom:12px;text-align:left;text-indent:0px;"><font style="padding-bottom:12px;text-align:left;font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;font-weight:bold;padding-right:48px;">&#8226;</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;font-weight:bold;">Nest moves to Google</font></div><div style="line-height:138%;padding-bottom:12px;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;">In February 2018, we announced that Nest will join forces with Google&#8217;s hardware team. Consequently, the financial results of Nest will be reported in the Google segment, with Nest revenues reflected in Google other revenues. Consolidated financial results will not be affected. </font></div><div style="line-height:138%;padding-bottom:12px;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;">In our Q1 2018 earnings release, we will recast segment information reflecting the Nest move from the Other Bets to the Google segment for all quarters of 2017.</font></div><div style="line-height:138%;padding-left:0px;padding-bottom:12px;text-align:left;text-indent:0px;"><font style="padding-bottom:12px;text-align:left;font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;font-weight:bold;padding-right:48px;">&#8226;</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;font-weight:bold;">Metrics for Google Network Members&#8217; properties revenues</font></div><div style="line-height:138%;padding-bottom:12px;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;">Historically, we have provided monetization metrics for Google Network Members&#8217; properties (Network) revenues consisting of the percentage change in paid clicks and cost-per-click. </font></div><div style="line-height:138%;padding-bottom:12px;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;">As our impression-based revenues have become a more significant driver of Network revenues growth, the percentage change in paid clicks and cost-per-click cover less of our total Network revenues.  As a result, in Q1 2018, we will transition our Network revenue metrics from percentage change in paid clicks and cost-per-click to percentage change in impressions and cost-per-impression. The impressions and cost-per-impression metrics will cover nearly all of our Network revenues. </font></div><div style="line-height:138%;padding-bottom:12px;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;">The monetization metrics for Google properties revenues will remain unchanged.</font></div><div style="line-height:138%;padding-bottom:12px;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;">To provide a basis for comparison, our Q1 2018 earnings release will include the percentage change in impressions and cost-per-impression for Network revenues for all quarters of 2017 and the percentage change in paid clicks and cost-per-click will be provided for the last time. </font></div><div style="line-height:138%;padding-bottom:12px;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;color:#3c4043;font-weight:bold;">Posted by Amie Thuener, Chief Accountant</font></div><div><br></div><div></div>	</body>
